<p>Brown and white granulated sugar are 97% to nearly 100% <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a>, respectively, with less than 2% water, and no dietary fiber, protein or fat (table). Brown sugar contains a moderate amount of iron (15% of the <a href="/wiki/Reference_Daily_Intake" title="Reference Daily Intake">Reference Daily Intake</a> in a 100 gram amount, see table), but a typical serving of 4 grams (one teaspoon), would provide 15 <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">calories</a> and a negligible amount of iron or any other nutrient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Because brown sugar contains 5–10% <a href="/wiki/Molasses" title="Molasses">molasses</a> reintroduced during processing, its value to some consumers is a richer flavor than white sugar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">Health effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg"><img alt="Text document with red question mark.svg" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>possibly contains inappropriate or misinterpreted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITE" title="Wikipedia:CITE">citations</a> that do not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:V" title="Wikipedia:V">verify</a> the text</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by checking for citation inaccuracies.</span> <small><i>(March 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-unreliable_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg"><img alt="Text document with red question mark.svg" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">Some of this article's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">listed sources</a> <b>may not be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliable</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help this article by looking for better, more reliable sources. Unreliable citations may be challenged or deleted.</span> <small><i>(March 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A 2003 <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a> technical report provided evidence that high intake of sugary drinks (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fruit_juice" title="Fruit juice">fruit juice</a>) increased the risk of <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a> by adding to overall <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_intake" title="Energy intake">energy intake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2003_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2003-69">[69]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empty_calorie" title="Empty calorie">'empty calories'</a> argument states that a diet high in added sugar will reduce consumption of foods that contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Essential_nutrient" title="Essential nutrient">essential nutrients</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Obesity_and_metabolic_syndrome">Obesity and metabolic syndrome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Obesity and metabolic syndrome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By itself, sugar is not a factor causing <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_syndrome" title="Metabolic syndrome">metabolic syndrome</a>, but rather – when over-consumed – is a component of unhealthy dietary behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2003_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2003-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Meta-analysis" title="Meta-analysis">Meta-analyses</a> showed that excessive consumption of sugar-sweetened beverages increased the risk of developing <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">type 2 diabetes</a> and metabolic syndrome – including weight gain and obesity – in adults and children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Addiction">Addiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Addiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A review published in 2014 suggests that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_addiction" title="Sugar addiction">sugar addiction</a> does not occur in humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperactivity">Hyperactivity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Hyperactivity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some studies report evidence of <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">causality</a> between high consumption of refined sugar and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperactivity" title="Hyperactivity">hyperactivity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> One review of low-quality studies of children consuming high amounts of <a href="/wiki/Energy_drink" title="Energy drink">energy drinks</a> showed association with higher rates of unhealthy behaviors, including smoking and alcohol abuse, and with hyperactivity and <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tooth_decay">Tooth decay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tooth decay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2003 WHO report stated that "Sugars are undoubtedly the most important dietary factor in the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_caries" title="Dental caries">dental caries</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2003_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2003-69">[69]</a></sup> A review of human studies showed that the incidence of caries is lower when sugar intake is less than 10% of total energy consumed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Alzheimer.27s_disease"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Alzheimer's_disease">Alzheimer's disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Alzheimer's disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Claims have been made of a sugar–<a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer's disease">Alzheimer's disease</a> connection, but there is inconclusive evidence that cognitive decline is related to dietary fructose or overall energy intake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recommended_dietary_intake">Recommended dietary intake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Recommended dietary intake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> recommends that both adults and children reduce the intake of free sugars to less than 10% of total energy intake, and suggests a reduction to below 5%. "Free sugars" include <a href="/wiki/Monosaccharide" title="Monosaccharide">monosaccharides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disaccharide" title="Disaccharide">disaccharides</a> added to foods, and sugars found in fruit juice and concentrates, as well as in honey and syrups. According to the WHO, "[t]hese recommendations were based on the totality of available evidence reviewed regarding the relationship between free sugars intake and body weight (low and moderate quality evidence) and dental caries (very low and moderate quality evidence)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_2015p4_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_2015p4-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 20, 2016, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration announced changes to the Nutrition Facts panel displayed on all foods, to be effective by July 2018. New to the panel is a requirement to list "Added sugars" by weight and as a percent of Daily Value (DV). For vitamins and minerals, the intent of DVs is to indicate how much should be consumed. For added sugars, the guidance is that 100% DV should not be exceeded. 100% DV is defined as 50 grams. For a person consuming 2000 calories a day, 50 grams is equal to 200 calories and thus 10% of total calories—the same guidance as the World Health Organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> To put this in context, most 12 ounce (335 mL) cans of soda contain 39 grams of sugar. In the United States, a government survey on food consumption in 2013–2014 reported that, for men and women aged 20 and older, the average total sugar intakes—naturally occurring in foods and added—were, respectively, 125 and 99 g/day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measurements">Measurements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Measurements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Various culinary sugars have different densities due to differences in particle size and inclusion of moisture.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domino_Sugar" title="Domino Sugar">Domino Sugar</a> gives the following weight to volume conversions (in <a href="/wiki/United_States_customary_units" title="United States customary units">United States customary units</a>):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Firmly packed brown sugar 1 lb = 2.5 cups (or 1.3 L per kg, 0.77 kg/L)</li>
<li>Granulated sugar 1 lb = 2.25 cups (or 1.17 L per kg, 0.85 kg/L)</li>
<li>Unsifted confectioner's sugar 1 lb = 3.75 cups (or 2.0 L per kg, 0.5 kg/L)</li></ul>
<p>The "Engineering Resources – Bulk Density Chart" published in <i>Powder and Bulk</i> gives different values for the bulk densities:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Beet sugar 0.80 g/mL</li>
<li>Dextrose sugar 0.62 g/mL ( = 620 kg/m^3)</li>
<li>Granulated sugar 0.70 g/mL</li>
<li>Powdered sugar 0.56 g/mL</li></ul>
<p><span id="History"></span>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Manufacturers of sugary products, such as <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a> and candy, and the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Association" title="Sugar Association">Sugar Research Foundation</a> have been accused of trying to influence consumers and medical associations in the 1960s and 1970s by creating doubt about the potential health hazards of sucrose overconsumption, while promoting <a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">saturated fat</a> as the main dietary risk factor in <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular diseases</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jama2016_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-jama2016-83">[83]</a></sup> In 2016, the criticism led to recommendations that diet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Policymaker" title="Policymaker">policymakers</a> emphasize the need for high-quality research that accounts for multiple <a href="/wiki/Biomarker" title="Biomarker">biomarkers</a> on development of cardiovascular diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jama2016_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-jama2016-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
